class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter_panorama_1.jpg" title="File:Exeter panorama 1.jpg"> </a></div>A panorama of the city taken from the roof of the north tower of the cathedral</div>\n</div></div>\n<p>Among the notable buildings in Exeter are:\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_buildings">Religious buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Religious buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ExeterCathedral-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/ExeterCathedral-4.jpg/220px-ExeterCathedral-4.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/ExeterCathedral-4.jpg/330px-ExeterCathedral-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/ExeterCathedral-4.jpg/440px-ExeterCathedral-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ExeterCathedral-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Cathedral" title="Exeter Cathedral">Exeter Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_War_Memorial" title="Devon County War Memorial">Devon County War Memorial</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Exeter#Religion" title="Exeter">Exeter \xc2\xa7&#160;Religion</a></div>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Cathedral" title="Exeter Cathedral">cathedral</a>, founded in 1050 when the bishop\'s seat was moved from the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Crediton" title="Crediton">Crediton</a> (birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a>) because Exeter\'s Roman walls offered better protection against "pirates", presumably <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Vikings</a>. A statue of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hooker_(theologian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Hooker (theologian)">Richard Hooker</a>, the 16th century <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> theologian, who was born in Exeter, has a prominent place in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Close,_Exeter" title="Cathedral Close, Exeter">Cathedral Close</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Nicholas_Priory" class="mw-redirect" title="St Nicholas Priory">St Nicholas Priory</a> in Mint Lane, the remains of a <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monastery</a>, later used as a private house and now a museum owned by the city council. The priory was founded in 1087 and was home to Benedictine monks for over 400 years, until it was closed and partly demolished by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>. The remaining buildings were then sold off in 1602 and became the home of the locally wealthy Hurst family. The property has been fully renovated by Exeter City Council, and the small garden area features Tudor plants and herbs<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>A number of medieval churches including <a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Mary_Steps,_Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="St Mary Steps, Exeter (page does not exist)">St Mary Steps</a> which has an elaborate clock.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Synagogue" title="Exeter Synagogue">Exeter Synagogue</a> is the third oldest synagogue in Britain, completed in 1763.</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter,_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg" class="image" title="A panorama of Exeter Cathedral and Cathedral Close"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg/900px-Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg" width="900" height="182" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg/1350px-Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg/1800px-Exeter%2C_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="13824" data-file-height="2798" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter,_Kathedrale_St._Peter_--_2013_--_1.jpg" title="File:Exeter, Kathedrale St. Peter -- 2013 -- 1.jpg"> </a></div>A panorama of Exeter Cathedral and <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Close,_Exeter" title="Cathedral Close, Exeter">Cathedral Close</a></div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secular_buildings">Secular buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Secular buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg/170px-The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg/255px-The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg/340px-The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg 2x" data-file-width="426" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_House_that_Moved_in_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1727313.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The House that Moved", West Street, Exeter</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Ruins" title="Ruins">ruins</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rougemont_Castle" title="Rougemont Castle">Rougemont Castle</a>, built soon after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Conquest">Norman Conquest</a>; later parts of the castle were still in use as a County Court until early 2006 when a new <a href="/wiki/Crown_Court" title="Crown Court">Crown Courts</a> building opened. A plaque near the ruined Norman gatehouse recalls the fate of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_Molland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alice Molland (page does not exist)">Alice Molland</a>, tried for <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a> at Exeter in 1685, and reputedly the last person in England to have been executed for that crime; others convicted of witchcraft had been hanged in Exeter in 1581, 1610, and 1682.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Guildhall" title="Exeter Guildhall">Guildhall</a>, which has medieval foundations and has been claimed to be the oldest municipal building in England still in use.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Mol\'s Coffee House, a historic building in the Cathedral Close.</li>\n<li>Tuckers\' Hall, a fine old building that is still used for smart functions.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Custom_House,_Exeter" title="Custom House, Exeter">Custom House</a> in the attractive <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Quay" title="Exeter Quay">Quay area</a>, which is the oldest brick building surviving in the city.</li>\n<li>"The House That Moved", a 14th-century <a href="/wiki/Tudor_style_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Tudor style architecture">Tudor</a> building, earned its name in 1961 when it was moved from its original location on the corner of Edmund Street in order for a new road to be built in its place. Weighing more than twenty-one tonnes, it was strapped together and slowly moved a few inches at a time to its present-day position.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parliament_Street,_Exeter" title="Parliament Street, Exeter">Parliament Street</a> in the city centre is one of the narrowest streets in the world.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Butts_Ferry" title="Butts Ferry">Butts Ferry</a>, an ancient <a href="/wiki/Cable_ferry" title="Cable ferry">cable ferry</a> across the River Exe.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wyvern_Barracks" title="Wyvern Barracks">Wyvern Barracks</a>, a former artillery barracks, dates back to about 1800.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Higher_Barracks,_Exeter" title="Higher Barracks, Exeter">Higher Barracks</a>, a former cavalry barracks, dates back to 1794.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_War_Memorial" title="Devon County War Memorial">Devon County War Memorial</a> in the Cathedral Close, designed by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Edwin_Lutyens" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Edwin Lutyens">Sir Edwin Lutyens</a> and unveiled in 1922 by <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Edward, Prince of Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Many of these are built in the local dark red <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a>, which gives its name to the castle and the park that now surrounds it (Rougemont means red hill). The pavements on Queen Street are composed of the rock <a href="/wiki/Diorite" title="Diorite">diorite</a> and exhibit <a href="/wiki/Feldspar" title="Feldspar">feldspar</a> crystals, while those around Princesshay are composed of <a href="/wiki/Granodiorite" title="Granodiorite">granodiorite</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northernhay_Gardens">Northernhay Gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Northernhay Gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Located just outside the castle, <a href="/wiki/Northernhay_Gardens" title="Northernhay Gardens">Northernhay Gardens</a> is the oldest public open space in England, being originally laid out in 1612 as a pleasure walk for Exeter residents.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg/220px-M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg/330px-M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg/440px-M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M5_Bridge_crosses_the_River_Exe_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1109085.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bridge carrying the <a href="/wiki/M5_motorway" title="M5 motorway">M5 motorway</a> across the <a href="/wiki/River_Exe" title="River Exe">River Exe</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/M5_motorway" title="M5 motorway">M5 motorway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and Exeter starts at <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, and connects at Bristol with the <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway" title="M4 motorway">M4</a> to London and <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a>. The older <a href="/wiki/A30_road" title="A30 road">A30 road</a> provides a more direct route to London via the <a href="/wiki/A303_road" title="A303 road">A303</a> and <a href="/wiki/M3_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M3 motorway (Great Britain)">M3</a>. The M5 is the modern lowest bridging point of the <a href="/wiki/River_Exe" title="River Exe">River Exe</a>. Going westwards, the <a href="/wiki/A38_road" title="A38 road">A38</a> connects Exeter to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and south east <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, whilst the A30 continues via <a href="/wiki/Okehampton" title="Okehampton">Okehampton</a> to north and west Cornwall. The cities of <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Somerset" title="Bath, Somerset">Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salisbury" title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Truro" title="Truro">Truro</a> can all be reached within 2 hours.\n</p><p>Travel by car in the city is often difficult with regular jams centred on the Exe Bridges area. Historically, the bridges were a significant bottleneck for holiday traffic heading to southwest England, leading to the construction of the first bypass in the mid-1930s over <a href="/wiki/Countess_Wear" title="Countess Wear">Countess Wear Bridge</a>, followed by the M5 in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-dcc_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dcc-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> To further address the problem of congestion in the city centre, <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Council" title="Devon County Council">Devon County Council</a> has current park and ride services and is considering the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Congestion_charge" class="mw-redirect" title="Congestion charge">congestion charges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exeter\'s main operator of local buses is <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_South_West" title="Stagecoach South West">Stagecoach South West</a>, which operates most of the services in the city. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dartline&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dartline (page does not exist)">Dartline</a> is a minor operator in the City. Former Cooks Coaches were taken over by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Stagecoach Devon">Stagecoach</a> forming Stagecoach South West. <a href="/wiki/Western_Greyhound" title="Western Greyhound">Western Greyhound</a> was also a main operator connecting Exeter to Cornwall, <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> and many different places in <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a> until being taken over by <a href="/wiki/First_South_West" title="First South West">First Devon &amp; Cornwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Citybus" title="Plymouth Citybus">Plymouth Citybus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_South_West" title="Stagecoach South West">Stagecoach South West</a> in March 2015.\n</p><p>The High Street, pedestrianised except for bus and bicycle traffic, serves as the main hub for local buses. Country and express services operate from the city\'s bus station, in Paris Street, which intersects the High Street at its eastern end; some also call at <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids railway station</a> for direct connection to train services.\n</p><p>Country bus services, mostly operated by Stagecoach, run from Exeter to most places in East and <a href="/wiki/North_Devon" title="North Devon">North Devon</a>, but some are very infrequent. Regional express services run to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bude" title="Bude">Bude</a>, and along the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a> to <a href="/wiki/Lyme_Regis" title="Lyme Regis">Lyme Regis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">Weymouth</a>, some operated by Stagecoach and others by <a href="/wiki/FirstGroup" title="FirstGroup">First Bus</a>. <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> operates long distance routes, for example to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a> and London.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg/220px-2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg/330px-2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg/440px-2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008_at_Exeter_St_Davids_-_station_frontage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exeter St Davids Railway Station</div></div></div>\n<p>Exeter is considered to be a rail hub within the south-west and is linked to most branch lines in Devon, including to <a href="/wiki/Riviera_Line" title="Riviera Line">Paignton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avocet_Line" title="Avocet Line">Exmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarka_Line" title="Tarka Line">Barnstaple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okehampton" title="Okehampton">Okehampton</a> (by a special service). This makes it possible to reach most stations in Devon directly from <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a>, although only during the summer months.\n</p><p>Exeter is served by three main railway stations. <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a> is served by all services and is a major <a href="/wiki/Interchange_station" title="Interchange station">interchange station</a> within the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Peninsula" title="South West Peninsula">South West Peninsula</a>\'s rail network, whilst <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Central_railway_station" title="Exeter Central railway station">Exeter Central</a> is more convenient for the city centre but served only by local services and the main line route to London Waterloo. In the south-west of the city, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Thomas_railway_station" title="Exeter St Thomas railway station">Exeter St Thomas</a> serves the western side of the city. There are also six suburban stations, <a href="/wiki/Topsham_railway_station" title="Topsham railway station">Topsham</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_James_Park_railway_station" title="St James Park railway station">St James Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polsloe_Bridge_railway_station" title="Polsloe Bridge railway station">Polsloe Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pinhoe_railway_station" title="Pinhoe railway station">Pinhoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digby_and_Sowton_railway_station" title="Digby and Sowton railway station">Digby &amp; Sowton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newcourt_(Exeter)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcourt (Exeter) railway station">Newcourt</a>, served only by local services.\n</p><p>There are two main line railway routes from Exeter to London, the faster <a href="/wiki/Reading_to_Taunton_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Reading to Taunton line">route via Taunton and Reading to London Paddington</a> and the slower <a href="/wiki/West_of_England_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="West of England Main Line">West of England Main Line</a> via <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Salisbury, England">Salisbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basingstoke" title="Basingstoke">Basingstoke</a> to <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a>. Another main line, the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Country_Route" title="Cross Country Route">Cross Country Route</a>, links Exeter with <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby" title="Derby">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>. <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> services continue westwards along the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter to Plymouth Line">Exeter to Plymouth Line</a>, variously serving <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">Torquay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>. Local branch lines run to <a href="/wiki/Paignton" title="Paignton">Paignton</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Riviera_Line" title="Riviera Line">Riviera Line</a>), <a href="/wiki/Exmouth,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Exmouth, Devon">Exmouth</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Avocet_Line" title="Avocet Line">Avocet Line</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Barnstaple" title="Barnstaple">Barnstaple</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Tarka_Line" title="Tarka Line">Tarka Line</a>). There is also a summer weekend service to <a href="/wiki/Okehampton" title="Okehampton">Okehampton</a> for access to <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_railway_of_the_LSWR" title="Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR">Exeter to Plymouth line of the London and South Western Railway (LSWR)</a> used to provide an alternative route via <a href="/wiki/Okehampton" title="Okehampton">Okehampton</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> to Exeter and the rest of the UK railway system until its closure in 1968. There are proposals to reopen the line from Okehampton, Tavistock to Bere Alston for a through service to Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On the night of 4 February 2014, amid high winds and extremely rough seas, part of the <a href="/wiki/South_Devon_Railway_sea_wall" title="South Devon Railway sea wall">South Devon Railway sea wall</a> at Dawlish was breached, washing away around 40 metres (130&#160;ft) of the wall and the ballast under the railway immediately behind and closing the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter to Plymouth Line">Exeter to Plymouth Line</a>. <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> began repair work<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and the line reopened on 4 April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In the wake of widespread disruption caused by damage to the mainline track at <a href="/wiki/Dawlish" title="Dawlish">Dawlish</a> by coastal storms in February 2014, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> are considering reopening the Bere Alston to Okehampton and Exeter section of the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_railway_of_the_LSWR" title="Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR">former LSWR line</a> as an alternative to the coastal route.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ExeterAirportUK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ExeterAirportUK.jpg/220px-ExeterAirportUK.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ExeterAirportUK.jpg/330px-ExeterAirportUK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/ExeterAirportUK.jpg/440px-ExeterAirportUK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ExeterAirportUK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exeter International Airport</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Airport" title="Exeter Airport">Exeter Airport</a> lies east of the city, and the local airline, previously called <a href="/wiki/Jersey_European" class="mw-redirect" title="Jersey European">Jersey European</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_European" class="mw-redirect" title="British European">British European</a> but now known as <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a>, is a significant local employer. It is also a base for <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomson Airways">Thomson Airways</a> with flights to <a href="/wiki/Faro_Airport" title="Faro Airport">Faro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mallorca" title="Mallorca">Mallorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a> and elsewhere. The airport offers a range of scheduled flights to British and Irish regional airports and <a href="/wiki/Charter_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter airline">charter</a> flights. Connections to international hubs began with <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle">Paris-Charles de Gaulle</a> in 2005 and later a daily service to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Schiphol Airport">Amsterdam Schiphol Airport</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canal">Canal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Canal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg/220px-Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg/330px-Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg/440px-Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Exeter_Canal_Basin_-_geograph.org.uk_-_238695.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exeter Canal Basin</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Canal" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter Canal">Exeter Canal</a> also known as the Exeter Ship Canal was first completed in about 1566,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> making it one of the oldest artificial waterways in Britain. It was cut to bypass <a href="/wiki/Weir" title="Weir">weirs</a> that had been built across the <a href="/wiki/River_Exe" title="River Exe">River Exe</a> to prevent trade in the city and to force boats to unload at <a href="/wiki/Topsham,_Devon" title="Topsham, Devon">Topsham</a> from where the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Devon" title="Earl of Devon">Earls of Devon</a> were able to exact large tolls to transport goods to Exeter. Originally 3 feet deep and 16 feet wide (0.9 m by 5 m), it ran 1.75 miles (2.82&#160;km) from just below the <a href="/wiki/Countess_Wear" title="Countess Wear">Countess Weir</a> to the centre of Exeter. It was later extended to Topsham, deepened and widened, and was successful until the middle of the 19th century since when its use gradually declined \xe2\x80\x93 the last commercial use was in 1972. However it is now widely used for leisure purposes, and the city basin is being included as part of a \xc2\xa324&#160;million redevelopment scheme.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Devon" title="List of schools in Devon">List of schools in Devon</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Laver_Building,_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg/170px-Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg/255px-Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg/340px-Laver_Building%2C_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg 2x" data-file-width="421" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Laver_Building,_University_of_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_148746.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Laver Building, University of Exeter</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> has two campuses in the city, both notable for their attractive parkland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is one of the largest employers in the city. Exeter is one of the four main sites of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> St Loye\'s School of Health Studies, which provides training in <a href="/wiki/Occupational_therapy" title="Occupational therapy">occupational therapy</a>, has now been incorporated into the University of Plymouth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The university includes the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter_Business_School" title="University of Exeter Business School">Business School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bill_Douglas_Cinema_Museum" title="Bill Douglas Cinema Museum">Bill Douglas Cinema Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wellcome" title="Henry Wellcome">Henry Wellcome</a> building for Biocatalysis, and, as of September 2018, the Exeter Centre for <a href="/wiki/Ellen_MacArthur_Foundation" title="Ellen MacArthur Foundation">Circular Economy</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_College,_Exeter" title="Exeter College, Exeter">Exeter College</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> college. It previously operated as the sole <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> for the entire <a href="/wiki/Maintained_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintained school">maintained school</a> sector in the city. However, in 2014 <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Mathematics_School" title="Exeter Mathematics School">Exeter Mathematics School</a> was established, a <a href="/wiki/Free_school_(England)" title="Free school (England)">free school</a> sixth form with a specialism in Mathematics.\n</p><p>For about 30 years the city of Exeter operated a <a href="/wiki/Maintained_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintained school">maintained school</a> system in which the divisions between phases came at different ages from most of the United Kingdom, with first, middle and high rather than infant, junior and secondary schools, so that children transferred between schools at the age of about 8 and 12 rather than 7 and 11.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> From 2005, however, it has adopted the more usual pattern, because of the pressures of the UK <a href="/wiki/National_Curriculum_(England,_Wales_and_Northern_Ireland)" title="National Curriculum (England, Wales and Northern Ireland)">National Curriculum</a>. The changeover back to the more typical structure led to a citywide, <a href="/wiki/Private_Finance_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Private Finance Initiative">PFI</a> funded, rebuilding programme for the high schools and led to the changing of names for some schools. Following the reorganisation there are 25 primary schools, four referral schools, three <a href="/wiki/Special_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Special school">special schools</a> and five secondary schools within Exeter.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The secondary schools are <a href="/wiki/Isca_Academy" title="Isca Academy">Isca Academy</a> (formerly Priory High School), <a href="/wiki/St_James_School,_Exeter" title="St James School, Exeter">St James School</a> (formerly St James High School), <a href="/wiki/St_Luke%27s_Science_and_Sports_College" title="St Luke&#39;s Science and Sports College">St Luke\'s Science and Sports College</a> (formerly Vincent Thompson High School), <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_Church_of_England_Aided_School" title="St Peter&#39;s Church of England Aided School">St Peter\'s Church of England Aided School</a> (a consolidation of the former Bishop Blackall High School for Girls and Heles High School for Boys), and <a href="/wiki/West_Exe_School" title="West Exe School">West Exe School</a> (formerly St Thomas High School).\n</p><p>The city has a number of independent schools, including <a href="/wiki/Exeter_School" title="Exeter School">Exeter School</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter_Cathedral_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Exeter Cathedral School (page does not exist)">Exeter Cathedral School</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Maynard_School" title="The Maynard School">The Maynard School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bramdean_School" title="Bramdean School">Bramdean School</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Wilfrid%27s_School,_Exeter" title="St Wilfrid&#39;s School, Exeter">St Wilfrid\'s School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Tutorial_College" title="Exeter Tutorial College">Exeter Tutorial College</a>.\n</p><p>There are specialist schools for pupils with sensory needs, including Exeter Royal Academy for Deaf Education, and the West of England School for the Partially Sighted.\n</p><p>The Atkinson Unit is a secure specialist residential and educational complex for children in care or <a href="/wiki/Detention_of_suspects" class="mw-redirect" title="Detention of suspects">remanded</a> by the courts.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Michael%27s_church,_and_Episcopal_building,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg/170px-St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg/255px-St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg/340px-St_Michael%27s_church%2C_and_Episcopal_building%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Michael%27s_church,_and_Episcopal_building,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_287157.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. Michael\'s Church &amp; Episcopal Building</div></div></div>\n<p>Numerous churches, and other religious buildings, are present in Exeter. Of which a majority belong to differing Christian denominations, with the exemption of an <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> cathedral. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Cathedral" title="Exeter Cathedral">Exeter Cathedral</a> is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Exeter" title="Bishop of Exeter">Bishop of Exeter</a>. The erection of the present building was completed in approximately 1400, and possesses the longest uninterrupted vaulted ceiling in England, as well as other noticeable characteristics. A collective of Anglican churches form the <a href="/wiki/Deanery_of_Christianity_(Exeter)" title="Deanery of Christianity (Exeter)">Exeter Deanery</a>.  \n</p><p>On the other hand, the Catholic community of Exeter occupy two Churches, the <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Church,_Exeter" title="Sacred Heart Church, Exeter">Sacred Heart</a> and the Blessed Sacrament, with congregations reflecting the nature of older and more recent immigration.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Synagogue" title="Exeter Synagogue">Exeter Synagogue</a>, located within a near proximity to Mary Arches Street, was completely erected in 1763. \n</p><p>Exeter\'s mosque and Islamic centre are located on York Road. The purpose-built mosque opened in 2011. \n</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">2001 census</a>, 69.12% of Exeter\xe2\x80\x99s population stated their religion as Christian, which is mildly lower than the regional average of 73.99% and the national average of 71.74%. Despite this, all other religions had exceeded the regional average at just under 1%. Although, they were much lower than the national average with the exemption of Buddhism. 20.45% of Exeter\xe2\x80\x99s population stated they had no religion, which was higher than the regional average of 16.75% and the national average of 14.59%. <sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglican_churches">Anglican churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Anglican churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_David%27s_church,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg/220px-St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg/330px-St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg/440px-St_David%27s_church%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_David%27s_church,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_213553.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. David\'s Church, Exeter</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/John_Betjeman" title="John Betjeman">John Betjeman</a> (writing in 1958) selects <a href="/wiki/St_David%27s_Church,_Exeter" title="St David&#39;s Church, Exeter">St David\'s</a> ("<a href="/wiki/W._D._Caroe" class="mw-redirect" title="W. D. Caroe">Caroe</a>\'s best church"), <a href="/wiki/St_Martin%27s_Church,_Exeter" title="St Martin&#39;s Church, Exeter">St Martin\'s</a> ("characteristic little city church, 15th century"), St Mary Steps ("medieval city church; font"), St Michael\'s ("Victorian, on a fine site"), and <a href="/wiki/St_Thomas,_Exeter" title="St Thomas, Exeter">St. Thomas\'s</a> ("fittings"). His coverage of St Mary Arches is more detailed: "worth seeing ... as the completest Norman church in Devon: beautifully light and airy after its restoration from the bombing in 1942. 18th-century altar arrangements. Memorials to Exeter worthies, 16th to 18th centuries."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The aforementioned collective of Anglican churches include St David\'s Church, located near to St. David\xe2\x80\x99s Station. The church was envisaged by <a href="/wiki/W._D._Caroe" class="mw-redirect" title="W. D. Caroe">W. D. Caroe</a>, with the windows being manufactured by Kempe &amp; Tower, and was later constructed between 1897 and 1900. A tower stands on the northeast side, with the overall design being described as \xe2\x80\x9chighly picturesque by Nikolaus Pevsner. \n</p><p>St Edmund-on-the-Bridge was built on the Exe Bridge ca. 1230\xe2\x80\x9340. Two arches of the bridge remain under the undercroft though the church was rebuilt in the Perpendicular style in 1835, using the old materials.\n</p><p>St Martin\'s is in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Close" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral Close">Cathedral Close</a>; the plan is odd, and there are numerous items of church furniture, though these are not of high aesthetic value. St Mary Arches is a Norman church with aisles. St Mary Steps was originally by the West Gate of the city; the font is Norman, and there is a remarkable early clock. St Michael, Heavitree was built in 1844\xe2\x80\x9346 and extended later in the century. <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_Church,_Exeter" title="St Pancras Church, Exeter">St Pancras</a> is of the 13th century and has a nave and chancel only; the font is Norman. The plan of <a href="/wiki/St_Petrocks_Church,_Exeter" class="mw-redirect" title="St Petrocks Church, Exeter">St Petroc\'s</a> church is highly unusual: a second chancel has been added facing north while the original chancel has another use and faces east. There are two aisles on the south, one of 1413 and another of the 16th century.\n</p><p>St Sidwell\'s church is by W. Burgess, 1812, in the Perpendicular style. <a href="/wiki/St_Stephens_Church,_Exeter" class="mw-redirect" title="St Stephens Church, Exeter">St Stephen\'s church</a> is partly of the 13th century but most of the structure is as rebuilt in 1826.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St_Michael_and_All_Angels_Church,_Exeter" class="mw-redirect" title="St Michael and All Angels Church, Exeter">St Michael and All Angels Church</a> on Mount Dinham has a spire which exceeds the height of the towers of Exeter Cathedral.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG/220px-St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG/330px-St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG/440px-St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_James_Park_-_Old_Grandstand.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_James_Park_(Exeter)" title="St James Park (Exeter)">St James Park</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City F.C.</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_Union">Rugby Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Rugby Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Chiefs" title="Exeter Chiefs">Exeter Chiefs</a> play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Park" title="Sandy Park">Sandy Park</a> stadium, located adjacent to junction 30 of the M5, and frequently achieve attendances of over 11,000 spectators. Sandy Park was constructed in September 2006 and cost \xc2\xa315 million. Exeter Chiefs relocated there from their previous stadium at the County Ground which had been used continually from 1905. <sup id="cite_ref-auto_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Exeter Chiefs achieved promotion in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_RFU_Championship" title="2009\xe2\x80\x9310 RFU Championship">2009\xe2\x80\x9310 season</a> following concessive victories against <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rugby" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol Rugby">Bristol</a> and have since remained within the highest division of English rugby, the <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Premiership" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviva Premiership">Aviva Premiership</a> <sup id="cite_ref-auto_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>. \n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Aviva_Premiership" class="mw-redirect" title="2011\xe2\x80\x9312 Aviva Premiership">2011\xe2\x80\x9312 season</a> of the Aviva Premiership, Exeter Chiefs  finished in fifth place, earning a spot in the <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a>. Exeter Chiefs won their first piece of silverware when they defeated Northampton 15-8 at Sandy Park in the 2014 LV Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>. Furthermore, Exeter Chiefs were crowned English champions in 2017, after defeating Wasps RFC in the Aviva Premiership final at Twickenham<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>. The city also has two other clubs: Wessex Rugby Club, which is located in Exwick, and Exeter Saracens Rugby Club,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> which is located in Whipton.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a> is Exeter\xe2\x80\x99s predominant Professional Association football club. They play their home games at St James Park, where they have remained since they were established in 1904. Originally, St James Park was a field used for fattening pigs. A redevelopment scheme was introduced in 2017, due to finish the year after, apparently providing a vastly increased fan experience. \n</p><p>Exeter City F.C became founder members of the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a>\'s new <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> (south) in 1920, but have never progressed beyond the third tier of the English football league system. In 2003, Exeter City F.C were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Football_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Conference">Conference</a> before reclaiming their Football League place in 2008 and achieving successive promotions to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a> in 2009. However, Exeter City F.C were relegated to League Two at the end of the 2011/12 season. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exeter Cricket Club administer three teams that play in the Devon Cricket League. The first of which plays in the Premier Division at first XI level and the next plays at second XI level. \n</p><p>Exeter Cricket Club play their home games at Country Ground where they have remained for a period exceeding 180 years. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rowing">Rowing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rowing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exeter <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">Rowing</a> Club enjoys an extraordinarily large amount of success both locally and nationally, and has a recorded history originating in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The City of Exeter Rowing Regatta is run annually in July, and is the eldest and largest regatta in the South West, with racing first recorded on the river in the 1860s.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Squash">Squash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Squash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Devon &amp; Exeter <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">Squash</a> club is one of the most active squash clubs in the region, annually hosting the Exeter Diamonds. A collective of world class players. Moreover, Devon and Exeter Squash Club has a strong membership, exacting standards and a notable junior team. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Speedway">Speedway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Speedway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exeter\'s <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">speedway</a> team, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Falcons" title="Exeter Falcons">Exeter Falcons</a>, was established in 1929 and were located at the County Ground until its permanent closure in 2005.\n</p><p>In a fixture during the 2004 season, they defeated <a href="/wiki/Rye_House_Cobras" title="Rye House Cobras">Rye House</a> by the maximum score of 75\xe2\x80\x9315. \n</p><p>At the site, Exeter Falcons member Jack Geran trained younger members in the art of the shale sport on a speedway training track in the late 1970s and early-1980s. Speedway was also staged briefly at tracks in <a href="/wiki/Alphington,_Devon" title="Alphington, Devon">Alphington</a> and Peamore after the Second World War.\n</p><p>The history of <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">Speedway</a> in Exeter up to the mid-1950s has been recorded in three books by Tony Lethbridge.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg/170px-Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg" width="170" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg/255px-Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg/340px-Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riddle-pyramid-comp.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Exeter Riddle Sculpture in Exeter High Street, created by artist Michael Fairfax and installed in 2005<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Book" title="Exeter Book">Exeter Book</a></i>, an anthology of Anglo Saxon poetry, is conserved in the vaults of Exeter Cathedral. The Exeter Book originates from the 10th century and is one of four manuscripts that between them encompass all surviving poetry composed in <a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a>. Predominantly, the Book incorporates shorter poems, several religious pieces, and a series of <a href="/wiki/Riddle" title="Riddle">riddles</a>, a handful of which are famously <a href="/wiki/Lewd" class="mw-redirect" title="Lewd">lewd</a>. A selection of the aforementioned riddles are inscribed on a highly polished steel obelisk situated in High Street, placed there on 30 March 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another famous piece of literature is the <i><a href="/wiki/Exeter_Domesday" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter Domesday">Exon Domesday</a></i>, a composite land and tax register of 1086. The piece contains a variety of administrative materials concerning the counties of Cornwall, Devon, Dorset, Somerset and Wiltshire. This piece is also conserved in Exeter Cathedral.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Numerous theatres occupy Exeter. One of which is the <a href="/wiki/Northcott_Theatre" title="Northcott Theatre">Northcott Theatre</a>. The Northcott Theatre is situated in the Streatham campus of the University of Exeter and is one of relatively few provincial English theatres to maintain its own <a href="/wiki/Repertory" class="mw-redirect" title="Repertory">repertory company</a>. This theatre is the successor to the former <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Exeter" title="Theatre Royal, Exeter">Theatre Royal, Exeter</a> which was permanently closed in 1962. \n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barnfield_Theatre_(geograph_4203993).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg/220px-Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg/330px-Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg/440px-Barnfield_Theatre_%28geograph_4203993%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barnfield_Theatre_(geograph_4203993).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Barnfield Theatre</div></div></div>\n<p>Another popular theatre in Exeter is the <a href="/wiki/Barnfield_Theatre" title="Barnfield Theatre">Barnfield Theatre</a>. Originally, the building was constructed as Barnfield Hall by Exeter Literary Society towards the end of the 19th century and converted in 1972. Currently, the theatre is a charity and is used as a venue for amateur and professional theatrical companies. \n</p><p>The Cygnet Theatre in Friars Walk is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Cygnet_Training_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Cygnet Training Theatre">Cygnet Training Theatre</a> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_Drama_Schools" title="Conference of Drama Schools">Conference of Drama Schools</a>. As well as performances given by students in training, this theatre also stages performances from visiting repertory companies and has a good reputation for quality events.\n</p><p>The Bike Shed Theatre and Cocktail Bar opened in September 2010 before permanently closing in March 2018. The Theatre was forced to close after failing to generate enough profit from the cocktail bar in order to operate the theatre. Fundamentally, the theatre offered intimate live music and performances and operated from basement premises in Fore Street. \n</p><p>Additionally, more innovative and contemporary performances, theatrical productions and dance pieces are programmed by Exeter Phoenix in Exeter City Centre and The Exeter Corn Exchange in Market Street.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(May 2010)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>There are two festivals each year, of all the arts but with a particular concentration of musical events: the annual "Vibraphonic"<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> festival, held in March provides a fortnight of soul, blues, jazz, funk, reggae and electronic music.\n</p><p>The largest orchestra based in Exeter is the EMG Symphony Orchestra<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> which frequently presents concerts at the University of Exeter and at Exeter Cathedral.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_Galleries">Museums and Galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Museums and Galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Memorial_Museum" title="Royal Albert Memorial Museum">Royal Albert Memorial Museum</a> in Queen Street is Exeter\xe2\x80\x99s predominant museum. The museum maintains its own collections of regional, national and international importance. Recently, the museum underwent an extensive refurbishment. It reopened on 14 December 2011, and was subsequently awarded the National Art Fund Prize \xe2\x80\x93 UK Museum of the Year 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The Museum also runs St Nicholas Priory in Mint Lane, near Fore Street.</li>\n<li>Additionally, the University of Exeter has an extensive fine art collection and an assortment of exhibition spaces across its Streatham campus. Showing a vibrant programme of exhibitions, performances, films and visual arts. The sculpture collection contains works by artists including Barbara Hepworth, Peter Thursby, Geoffrey Clark and Elaine M. Goodwin. It can be located using the Sculpture Trail.</li>\n<li>Exeter Phoenix is one of South West England\xe2\x80\x99s leading contemporary arts venues. The venue occupies the former university site in Gandy Street and programmes international, national and outstanding regional artists.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spacex_(art_gallery)" title="Spacex (art gallery)">Spacex (art gallery)</a>, a contemporary arts organisation, programmes exhibitions of contemporary art and promotes artist-led projects, events and research.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Express_and_Echo" class="mw-redirect" title="Express and Echo">Express and Echo</a></i>, twice-weekly with a Monday and Thursday edition.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Trewman%27s_Exeter_Flying_Post" title="Trewman&#39;s Exeter Flying Post">Exeter Flying Post</a></i>, published weekly. Originally discontinued in 1917, but was revived in 1976 as an alternative community magazine.</li>\n<li><i>The <a href="/wiki/Western_Morning_News" title="Western Morning News">Western Morning News</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> printed daily regional paper.</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Exepos%C3%A9" title="Exepos\xc3\xa9">Exepos\xc3\xa9</a></i>, the University\'s student newspaper, printed fortnightly.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Devon" title="BBC Radio Devon">BBC Radio Devon</a> broadcasts to Exeter locally on FM (95.8) and AM (990 AM/MW), although the majority of programming originates in Plymouth. In the evenings, BBC Radio Devon joins the South West Regional service. <a href="/wiki/Heart_South_West" title="Heart South West">Heart South West</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Gemini_FM" class="mw-redirect" title="Gemini FM">Gemini FM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devonair" class="mw-redirect" title="Devonair">Devonair</a>, broadcasts on 97.0 FM, with <a href="/wiki/East_Devon" title="East Devon">East Devon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torbay" title="Torbay">Torbay</a> utilising their own frequencies. Both Heart South West and BBC Devon broadcast from the St. Thomas transmitter. AM radio is broadcast from Pearce\'s Hill located at J31 of the M5. \n</p><p>Other radio stations include <a href="/wiki/Exeter_FM" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter FM">Exeter FM</a>, an easy listening station broadcasting on 107.3 FM, Phonic.FM which provides a "no adverts no playlist" alternative on 106.8 FM or online at www.phonic.fm, VI, a station broadcasting from the West of England School and College on 1386 AM/MW.\n</p><p>Additionally, Exeter University has a well established student station, <a href="/wiki/Xpression_FM" title="Xpression FM">Xpression FM</a>, which broadcasts on 87.7 FM using two low-powered transmitters, although it can be heard over much of the north of the city.\n</p><p>The local <a href="/wiki/Commercial_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial radio">commercial radio</a> station is <a href="/wiki/107.3_Radio_Exe" title="107.3 Radio Exe">Radio Exe</a>. The local <a href="/wiki/Community_radio" title="Community radio">community radio</a> station is <a href="/wiki/Phonic_FM" title="Phonic FM">Phonic FM</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Both <a href="/wiki/BBC_Spotlight" class="mw-redirect" title="BBC Spotlight">BBC Spotlight</a> and ITV Westcountry provide Exeter with regional news outputs. BBC Spotlight is broadcast from Plymouth and ITV Westcountry is broadcast from Bristol. Although, both services do have newsrooms in Exeter. The St Thomas and <a href="/wiki/Stockland_Hill_transmitting_station" title="Stockland Hill transmitting station">Stockland Hill transmitting station</a> both provide the city\xe2\x80\x99s coverage with both transmitters having completed the <a href="/wiki/Digital_switchover" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital switchover">digital switchover</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns">Twin towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Twin towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Piazza_Terracina,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg/170px-Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg/255px-Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg/340px-Piazza_Terracina%2C_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piazza_Terracina,_Exeter_-_geograph.org.uk_-_236121.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Piazza Terracina, Exeter, named after <a href="/wiki/Terracina" title="Terracina">Terracina</a>, Italy</div></div></div>\n<p>Exeter is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> in France,<sup id="cite_ref-Archant_twinning_3_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archant_twinning_3-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Bad Homburg">Bad Homburg</a> in Germany, <a href="/wiki/Yaroslavl" title="Yaroslavl">Yaroslavl</a> in Russia, and <a href="/wiki/Terracina" title="Terracina">Terracina</a> in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-Exeter_twinning_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exeter_twinning-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Exeter&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: See
